Wu Liande Reports on the Past Year

Harbor Quarantine Achievements

Thanks to the Assistance of All Parties

Reducing Human Mortality

The Shanghai Harbor Quarantine Administration held its third anniversary banquet at the East Asia Restaurant last night at 8:30 PM. More than a hundred guests attended, including Tang Hai'an, Qia Qing, and Wang Lai. During the banquet, Chairman Dr. Wu De gave a detailed report on the work of the year. American Consul General Mr. Cunningham gave a response. The banquet ended at 11 PM in high spirits. Dr. Wu's speech is recorded below:

"I am deeply honored by your presence and guidance tonight. On behalf of the Shanghai Harbor Quarantine Administration, I extend my welcome. In the past year, all our measures and work have been greatly aided by the consular corps, the shipping industry, and related organizations, enabling us to achieve some success. The future is long, and we still hope for your wise guidance. Now, I will briefly outline the work of this year."

(A) Overview of Wusong: At the beginning of this year, the Shanghai Incident suddenly broke out. Our medical officer in Wusong initially made every effort to continue working as usual. However, forced by the intense artillery fire, he eventually evacuated to Shanghai. All the clinics in Wusong and the nearby Xingyu were burned down by the artillery fire. Fortunately, the Shanghai Harbor Quarantine Hospital in Pudong remained intact. Recently, it has even installed its own electricity. New buildings have been constructed at the original site of the Wusong office, and the clinic has resumed normal operations there since the beginning of this month.

(B) Quarantine Work: Since February 1st of this year, all ships arriving in Shanghai have been subject to quarantine upon arrival. This method has been satisfactory and has not caused delays to navigation. Even during the cholera epidemic this summer, we inspected about 25 ships every day. All the quarantine personnel of our office worked diligently, and the results were quite good. Here is a list of the ships inspected in Shanghai and their tonnage from January 1st to December 10th of this year:

Inspected Ships

Number of Ships　　　　Tonnage

China　 108　　　 196,098

UK　 755　 5,138,396

USA　 210　 2,287,675

Japan　 712　 3,666,880

Norway　 148　　 642,497

Finland　 57　　 410,291

Germany　 82　　 631,847

France　 58　　 723,381

Other　 114　　 770,875

(C) Ship Fumigation: The ship fumigation department of our office has also been very active this year. A total of 9,733 ships were fumigated, with a total hold tonnage of 1,615,431 tons. The fumigation drugs used have been quite effective. This year, a total of 2,867 dead rats were collected during ship fumigation, compared to 2,086 last year.

(D) Rat and Flea Research: Since the beginning of this year, our office has begun to study the rats and fleas in Shanghai. This is of great significance to the issue of plague. From January to the end of November, a total of 691 live rats were captured, and 314,155 fleas were collected from the rats. However, no plague bacteria were found in the captured live rats or the dead rats collected during ship fumigation. Our branch offices in Guangzhou and Xiamen are also conducting similar work, under the commission of the League of Nations Health Organization's Plague Research Department.

(E) Cooperation Among Departments: The epidemic prevention department, the ship fumigation department, and the medical department of our office all have interconnected work. Let me give an example: When a ship arrives in Shanghai from a plague-infected port, it is first inspected by the medical officer of the epidemic prevention department. If cholera is found, the ship is detained, and the ship fumigation department handles the disinfection. The medical department then handles the patients and contacts, and performs cholera vaccination and bacterial examinations.

Page 12

After all procedures are completed, the ship is released. This is an example of cooperation among the departments.

(F) Purchasing New Vessels: For the convenience of our work, our office began building a new ship last year, named "Hua Tuo," which will be put into use within one or two weeks. Including the previous ones, we will have a total of three steamers and two fumigation boats.

(G) Establishing Quarantine Branch Offices: Our office originally had a plan to unify the quarantine affairs of all seaports in the country. Therefore, the quarantine affairs of Tianjin, Tanggu, and Qinhuangdao were gradually taken back from the local customs offices in April. The Wuhan branch office has also started ship fumigation work, which is very convenient for ships in the Wuhan area. The Xiamen branch office has the best performance and serves as a model for other branch offices. When smallpox and cholera were prevalent in the area and other ports, the branch office was able to handle the situation with ease in the shortest amount of time. New migrant housing is under construction, and the new steamer that was added has also begun construction.

(H) Preventing the Spread of Cholera: The widespread and ferocious nature of the cholera epidemic this year is rare in Chinese history. The first case of cholera in Shanghai was discovered on April 26th, and the last case was discovered on October 17th, with a total epidemic period of 175 days. There were a total of 4,295 patients and 318 deaths, including 75 foreign patients and 20 deaths. Therefore, the mortality rate for foreigners was 26%, while the mortality rate for Chinese was only 7%. The incidence rate for Chinese was only 10 per 1,000 people, while the incidence rate for foreigners was 15 per 1,000 people. Shanghai was able to achieve this good result of a minimum mortality rate thanks to the concerted efforts of various health organizations and the public. In addition to inspecting ships, our office also vaccinated thousands of people.

(I) Rescuing Refugees and Wounded Soldiers: During the Shanghai Incident, refugees and wounded soldiers moved from the war zone to the public and French concessions. Our office immediately sent medical officers to work with various groups to rescue them. There were a total of 56 shelters, accommodating about 22,000 refugees. We also participated in the treatment of wounded soldiers and injured refugees at the Meibige Road Hospital. The hospital was established at the beginning of the war and closed at the end of April.

One more point I must mention to you: In October of this year, Dr. Hu Hongji, the director of the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, was killed in a car accident. My colleagues and I were deeply saddened by the news. Dr. Hu was not only a health expert, but also made many contributions to public health. Both last year and this year, Dr. Hu greatly assisted in the cholera prevention campaign and the Cholera Prevention Institute I presided over. His contributions should not be forgotten or left unrecorded. Finally, I must declare that all the work of our office has been fully supported by the Shanghai and other port customs offices, the consular corps, and the shipping industry. The news media has also done its best to publish information to increase public health knowledge, for which we are deeply grateful.

China Merchants Bureau North Wharf Operates As Usual

He Tiehua Arrives at Wharf Yesterday to Take Office

Refuses He Group's Petition to the Head Office

After all the employees of the China Merchants Bureau North Wharf opposed He Tiehua's return to the North Wharf, refused to hand over, and all resigned, General Manager Liu Hongsheng, in order to maintain passenger and cargo handling, specially dispatched personnel yesterday morning to work with the employees who were working as usual to take charge of the tallying department to ensure that passengers and cargo would not be affected. The newly appointed wharf director He Tiehua arrived at the wharf as usual to take office, and the Huishan Police Station increased the number of Chinese and foreign armed detectives stationed at the North Station to protect the work. The employees of the Fifth Wharf rejected the He Group, held a large meeting at the Jinliyuan Wharf at 9:00 AM yesterday and resolved: (1) to establish a presidium with 11 chairpersons; (2) to establish five departments, including general affairs, secretary, publicity, transportation, and maintenance, to allocate work; (3) to decide to petition the board of directors at 3:00 PM in the afternoon to request that they uphold justice in order to remedy the situation and achieve the purpose of withdrawing the order. At 3:00 PM in the afternoon, more than 120 members of the He Group rejection group gathered at Jinliyuan Wharf and walked to the head office to petition. After arriving at the office, they gathered in the auditorium. Jiang Yinkui, Zhang Guiqing, Wang Xingcun, Shan Xishou, Yao Lianbai, and others were selected to go to the board of directors. After the Laozha Police Station received the report, they immediately dispatched a large number of Chinese and foreign armed detectives to guard the area. The board of directors dispatched General Manager Liu Hongsheng to reply to the employee representatives, saying that the China Merchants Bureau is a state-run shipping industry, and advised them to work with peace of mind as soon as possible. As for the employees of the North Wharf, if they have no major faults at ordinary times, they will never be dismissed. If they commit major faults, they will be dismissed. They also set a deadline of the 16th to resume work, otherwise, in order to maintain business, they will all be dismissed. The two sides remained at odds until 5:00 PM, and then they dispersed and returned to the Fifth Wharf Workers' Association to discuss and decided to convene an emergency general meeting at 9:00 PM to discuss how to proceed.

The Reason Why Kong Xiangxi Is Staying in the United States

Unable to Return in Time to Participate in the Third Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee

Kong Xiangxi, the special envoy for the inspection of European and American industries, set sail on September 2nd, as reported in various newspapers. According to a New York communication, Kong arrived in San Francisco in late September and transferred to the American Transcontinental Railway to go to the Eastern United States. Along the way, he passed through Dingbao, St. Louis, and Chicago, and stayed in each place for three to five days, examining in detail the farms, factories, and trading markets in each place. He arrived in New York in early October. In addition to investigating the industrial and commercial situation there, he repeatedly responded to invitations from leaders from all walks of life and Chinese and foreign groups to attend lectures, giving a good impression to the people of that country. In late October, when he transferred to Washington, D.C., it was the time of the presidential election. President Hoover was about to go on a tour, so he made time to meet and talk for more than half an hour. Both sides expressed their sincere desire to enhance Sino-American relations. Later, he met with Secretary of State Stimson several times, and they had a very harmonious conversation. In addition, he visited the Undersecretaries of the Department of Agriculture, the Department of Commerce, and the Department of Labor, and visited their headquarters and affiliated agencies, examining their organization and administration in detail. In early November, Kong returned to New York. He originally planned to go to Europe immediately, but he happened to meet the Democrat Franklin D. Roosevelt, who was elected as the next president. Kong had direct or indirect relations with various important figures of the Democratic Party, so he could not avoid contacting them briefly. In addition, factories in Pittsburgh and other places were still inviting him to visit, so the date of his trip to Europe had to be postponed slightly. It is heard that the government will hold the Third Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee in mid-December, and has telegraphed Kong to return to the country to attend. In this situation, it is feared that he will not be able to return in time.

The Third Edition of Shenbao Monthly is Published

Since the publication of the inaugural issue of Shenbao Monthly in July of this year, it has been well received by all sectors of society and has been selling exceptionally well. The first edition of the first and second issues sold out in mid-September. Therefore, a second edition was printed in mid-October. However, by the beginning of last month, not only had the second edition of the first and second issues sold out, but the first edition of the third and fourth issues had also sold out at the same time. However, subscribers are still very enthusiastic and are requesting to subscribe from the inaugural issue. In order to repay the kind intentions of the annual commemorative subscribers, the company has specially reprinted the first and second issues in a third edition, and added a second edition of the third and fourth issues to meet the demand. It is now heard that the third edition and the second edition of the monthly magazines have been published, so those who wish to subscribe from the inaugural issue of the magazine will not have the regret of missing out. It is also heard that the special New Year's issue of the magazine has rich content and has been sent for typesetting early. It will be published in early next month. The retail price will be increased, but subscribers will not be charged extra, in order to show preferential treatment.

The Kailiping Mining Company Will Hold a Shareholders Meeting in London

Full Year Account Slightly Published

Pay a Final Dividend of Five Percent

The English Kailiping Mining Company Limited announced that, for the purpose of notifying, the company is scheduled to hold an annual general meeting of shareholders in London on December 20, 1932, at which time the directors' report and the full-year account ending June 30, 1932, will be publicly announced. The directors' report is excerpted on the left:

The net profit for the year amounted to £119,836, calculated as follows: the balance of profits due from the Kailiping Mining Administration, plus interest in China, totaled £256,032, interest in Europe was £21,552, management fees earned were £6,000, miscellaneous receipts were £110, and the previous balance (less miscellaneous items) was £1,202. The above receipts totaled £284,896. Deducting the following expenses: expenses in Europe were £14,209, the value of new interest coupons and new interest bonds for bearer shares was £4,582, directors' fees were £6,905, exchange water consumption was £18,569, income tax was £71,795, and the dividend prepaid on May 4, 1932 was £49,000. The total was £165,060. The net profit was £119,836. The directors proposed that the net profit be distributed as follows: pay a final dividend of five percent (tax-free), totaling £98,000, and transfer £21,836 to the next account, for a total of £119,836.

Minutes of the Executive and Supervisory Committee of the Lawyers Association

One Hundred and Twenty-Sixth Meeting

The Shanghai Lawyers Association convened its 126th joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees at its headquarters at the intersection of Avenue Petain and Rue Lafayette in the French Concession last night at 7:00 PM. The attending members were Zhu Fuqiu, Shen Junru, Chen Xurui, Jiang Jiemin, Shi Liang, Zhou Shidi, Liu Shifang, Zhang Zhirang, Tang Hao, Shitou, Zhang Zhixue, Yang Zhihao, and Li Shirui. Li Shirui was elected as chairman, and Dai Jiguang recorded the minutes. The resolutions are recorded below: (1) The standing committee member reported that Song Yundi attended to explain the case of the illegal service of a notice by the Shanghai Second Special District Court. Song Yundi then presented the situation of the case. (Resolution) Regarding the part of the case involving the crime of the bailiff, Song Yundi should file a private prosecution. Regarding the part of the case involving the supervision of the bailiff, the association should send a letter to the Second Special District Court requesting that it pay attention to rectification. (2) The standing committee member reported that a telegram was sent to the central Yuanbu requesting that it formulate jury regulations regarding crimes of state affairs. The draft of the telegram was submitted for discussion. (Resolution) Approved and sent. (3) The Shanghai First Special District Court prosecutor sent a letter informing the gongbu bureau of the investigation into the situation of the Zheng Wenxiang fraud case, requesting discussion. (Resolution) File for record. (4) The Shanghai Document Agency replied that it would follow the letter and advertise that legal events would not be included in the scope of the agency's business. (Resolution) File for record. (5) The Lawyers Association sent a letter requesting an on-the-spot investigation of the actual situation of the judiciary. (Resolution) In addition to forwarding the letter to the members for soliciting investigation materials in order to collect opinions and report them, a special committee should be organized. The committee should have nine members (five elected from the executive and supervisory committee, and four non-executive and supervisory committee members). Li Shirui, Shen Junru, Lu Dingkui, Zhang Zhengxue, Liu Shifang, Yu Zhongluo, Lu Shaozong, Zhong Hongsheng, and Cha Renwei were elected as members on the spot. (6) Member Zhang Zhenwan sent a letter inquiring whether a lawyer could refuse to testify when summoned as a witness. (Resolution) Reply to the member that according to law, people have the obligation to testify and cannot refuse. (7) Members Wang Shaoji and Lu Qingtian sent a letter reporting that the Chongming County Women and Children Relief Association published an insult to the reputation of lawyers, requesting that a letter be sent to the Chongming County Government to instruct the association to correct the error and forward the case to the Judicial Yuan for interpretation. (Resolution) Reply to the members Wang and others that the reported sections do not raise legal issues, and that the members can send a letter to correct the misunderstanding of the lawyer's duties. (8) Member Wei Wenhan sent a letter reporting that he planned to collect a public fee of 1,000 taels for handling foreign-related cases, requesting review and certification. (Resolution) Reply to the member that according to the regulations of Article 31, Paragraph 2 of the association's rules, the prescribed maximum amount has not been exceeded. (9) Citizen Zhang Yuntu sent a letter reporting that Dai Yuanpei impersonated a lawyer, requesting that it be banned. (Resolution) Handed over to the supervisory committee for investigation and verification. (10) Lawyers Quan Bin, Wu Peiran, Tang Shizhen, Zhou Chaogang, Hua Maosheng, Jiang Haoshi, Ning Boqing, Xue Dubi, Zhang Zhiben, and others filed a request to join the association. (Resolution) Approved. The meeting adjourned late at night after the discussion.

Thugs Assault Sanyou Factory Workers

Workers Chen Jintang and others are seriously injured

Ten Assailants Arrested and Sent to Court

The labor dispute at the Sanyou Industrial Society in Yinxiang Port, Shanghai East, has lasted nearly a year. Although the municipal government has mediated, the court has ruled, and various parties have made well-intentioned mediation attempts, the capital side has not accepted them, leading to an unresolved situation. Unexpectedly, yesterday morning, for some unknown reason, more than twenty thugs suddenly appeared and beat workers such as Chen Jintang, causing injuries. The details are as follows:

Sudden Appearance of Thugs

At around 10 a.m. yesterday morning, while the factory workers were having lunch inside the factory, more than twenty thugs, including Wu Bingyi, Bao Yuqing, and Yang Changlin, carrying weapons, sneaked into the factory building. Without asking any questions, they started beating anyone they saw. The workers were caught off guard and had no chance to resist. As a result, Chen Jintang's head was injured by an axe, Zhou Shengfu suffered severe injuries to his waist and chest, Wu Songshou's left leg bone was broken by an iron bar, and several others suffered minor injuries.

Arrest of Assailants

When the assault occurred, fortunately, the Fourth Precinct of the Fifth District and the police detachment stationed at the factory heard the alarm and immediately worked together to arrest the assailants. Ten people were apprehended, including Yang Changlin, Yang Mingfa, Luo Jifu, Luo Ailin, Bu Zhengcai, Zhang Xiucai, Lin Xianshou, Wang Xueming, Zhang Huagui, and Luo Shengfu. They were taken to the station along with the injured workers.

Transfer to the Court

After questioning by the police station chief, the case was deemed criminal and was immediately transferred to the local court for disposal with a written report. The assailants were temporarily detained. Meanwhile, a forensic doctor examined the injuries of the injured workers, and they were allowed to seek medical treatment at the hospital themselves. It is reported that the procuratorate has decided to file a public prosecution.

Route Change for Bus Line No. 7

Facilitates North-South Transportation in the Western District

The Public Omnibus Company of the Public Concession, in order to facilitate the north-south line transportation in the western district, has obtained permission from the Public Works Department to change the route of Bus Line No. 7. It will now travel from the intersection of Haig Road and Hongqiao Road to Jing'an Temple, then onto Great Western Road, turning into Avenue Road, passing Jiaozhou Road, Rue Robert, and Xiaoshadu Road, until the intersection of Yichang Road. Previously, Bus Line No. 7 went to Jing'an Temple and then via Yu Garden Road and Bubbling Well Road to Wujiaochang. Now that Route A buses are already running in the Yu Garden Road area and are sufficient to carry passengers, Bus Line No. 7 can be rerouted.

Good Health Status in the Public Concession

The Public Health Director's report to the Board of Directors for November stated that the death rate among foreigners in the concession this month was 10.17, compared to 18.34 in the same month last year. The death rate among Chinese was 13.23, compared to 14.80 in the same month last year. Therefore, the health status of this port can be considered exceptionally good.

Rare Infectious Diseases The statistics for infectious diseases do not show anything particularly noteworthy, except for a slight increase in scarlet fever. Pulmonary tuberculosis and intestinal diseases remain as common as usual. The number of diphtheria cases among Chinese is quite high, while the number among foreigners is lower than in previous years. There are not many cases of smallpox, but vaccination work is being actively carried out. Within the month, 14,649 people were vaccinated by vaccination vehicles, and 8,419 people were vaccinated by various health sub-bureaus.

Pathological Laboratory Research The results of this month's research show that splenitis is quite common in slaughtered cattle. The pharmaceutical section produced 161 grams of bovine pulp this month and issued 34,560 doses of vaccine and 199 doses of micro-Ranson's emulsion. The laboratory received 1,261 specimens for microbiological examination and 239 specimens for analysis this month. The analysis work included diphtheria, meningitis, malaria, etc. The Pasteur treatment room had 52 patients this month, including three from other ports. There were no deaths among those treated.

Food Supply Milk production averaged 24,425 pounds per day. Thirty-six samples were tested, of which five were unsanitary, two were deficient in fat, one was adulterated with water, and three were mixed with buffalo milk. Ninety-nine samples were analyzed, of which eleven were unqualified, but all came from Class B or unregistered dairy farms. The number of cattle slaughtered this month increased, while the number of other livestock decreased, but all were higher than the average for the previous year. Business at various vegetable markets was quite good. Bakeries and food stores have improved significantly.

Hygiene Division Work With the arrival of winter, fly and mosquito control work has decreased, while vaccination is very busy. Mosquito breeding this year has lasted for a long time, probably due to the warmer weather. To check the sanitary conditions of schools receiving subsidies, an inspector has been assigned to take charge of this matter.

German僑 Celebrate Dr. Otte Mann's Birthday

His Friends Present Him with a Complete Collection of Song Dynasty Li Xue Classics

Dr. Otte Mann, a professor at Tongji University in Wusong, has been in China for many years. He has been immersed in Chinese studies and has a deep understanding of our country's literature. He has authored many works that have long been famous both in China and abroad. Since the European War, Dr. Mann has been in charge of the middle school department of Tongji University, patiently guiding and teaching in a systematic way. His students all feel his nurturing influence. The 16th of this month was Dr. Mann's 50th birthday. Dr. Mann's friends in Shanghai held a celebration for him yesterday at the Astor House Hotel, raising their glasses to offer him birthday wishes. They also knew that Dr. Mann was dedicated to books and classics, so they made great efforts to search and obtain a complete collection of Song Dynasty Li Xue classics, presenting it to Dr. Mann to peruse and commemorate. It is reported that the German Consul General in Shanghai, Feng Lide, Consul Bai Rende, and other famous German僑 were present at yesterday's grand banquet.

Zhenhai Electricity Company Temporarily Does Not Cut Off Power

Respecting the Intentions of the Local Authorities

Decision to Continue Maintenance Method

The Zhenhai Electricity Company previously decided to cut off power starting on the 16th of this month because users were unwilling to pay the actual usage fees, which affected the company's income. A meeting of all promoters and shareholders was convened on the 4th of this month to discuss the matter. After hearing the news, the various party, government, military, and police agencies in the county believed that electricity was very important for maintaining security during the current winter defense period in Zhenhai. They jointly sent a letter to the promoter, Fu Xiaoan, requesting that he continue to maintain the power supply. After receiving the letter, Fu held a general meeting of all parties at the Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association yesterday afternoon to discuss the matter. First, Chairman Wu Yaqin reported on the letters from the director of the Water Police Bureau, the commander of the Fort, the commander of the garrison battalion, the members of the Party Department, the magistrate of Zhenhai County, and the director of the Public Security Bureau. After discussion, it was generally agreed that the heads of various agencies had expressed their willingness to assist the company in the shortest possible time, and that they had also ordered that the actual amount owed be paid in full, which would alleviate most of the difficulties faced by the company. Next, Qian Zhongjun, Zhu Huanwen, Xie Weishan, Yu Shouchun, Dai Chengzhi, Zhou Jianhan, and others successively made proposals, and the following resolutions were unanimously passed: 1. In order to respect the intentions of the heads of various agencies, the power supply will be continued for another half month. 2. Within this half month, all users who owe fees must pay the full amount in order to clear the procedures. 3. If users still cannot pay the fees owed within half a month, the power supply will be cut off starting on January 1st of next year and will not be continued. 4. If users can pay the fees owed before the end of this year, the trial operation will be continued for another three months. 5. If the trial operation proceeds smoothly and actual usage is paid for, then further efforts will be made to continue soliciting shares and paying the money to formally establish the company; otherwise, the operation will be terminated after the trial period expires. 6. All users, regardless of who they are, will pay for actual usage and there will be no discounts or deductions forever. 7. The above resolutions will be submitted to the Jiangsu Construction Department and the Zhenhai County Government for record, and will be sent to various agencies and legal entities for reference. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Shanghai Public Utility Bureau Auctions Cargo Ship

Confiscated for Dodging Taxes

The Shanghai South Shipping Office of the Municipal Public Utility Bureau previously discovered a cargo ship with the serial number 5446. The stamped serial number and the ship's classification did not match, indicating that a lower-grade license had been used in an attempt to reduce taxes. The bureau confiscated the ship in accordance with the city's regulations on cracking down on cargo ships. It is reported that the municipal government has approved the public sale of the ship at the Shanghai South Shipping Office (Dongjiadu Wharf) at 10 a.m. on the 17th of this month. The proceeds will be remitted to the municipal treasury. Those who wish to purchase the ship can go to the office at that time to view the ship and make arrangements.

Minutes of the Executive Committee Meeting of the Roads Association

The China National Road Construction Association held an executive committee meeting yesterday. Attendees included Xu Shiying, Wang Zhengting, Zhu Shaoping, Xiang Kangyuan, Wu Kaisheng, Yin Ruli, Zhao Jinqing, and Wu Shan (also acting for Xu Yuan). Chairman Wang Zhengting (Xu Shiying was publicly elected as chairman before Wang Zhengting arrived) presided over the meeting. The following resolutions were passed: 1. General Manager Wu Shan reported that the solicitation for the opening of the General Assembly had been going on for a long time and should be concluded as soon as possible. It was resolved to hold a celebration and commendation ceremony on January 3rd, to be determined by the chairman, and to present commemorative gifts to the teams listed in the front. Approved as is. 2. The Chief reported that Committee Member Li Zushen of the National Government's Water Disaster Relief Committee attended the meeting yesterday and invited them to survey the dike construction in Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Hubei provinces. The dikes were wide, high, and strong, and the project was of great benefit to the country's economy and people's livelihood. After consultation with Committee Member Li, it was proposed to change the project of the万里long dike on the north and south banks into万里堤路, which could both protect the dike and facilitate transportation, benefiting both water and land transportation. The drafting and design of engineers, soldiers, and road builders, as well as the future inter-provincial automobile transportation plans across the dike, are being submitted to the Executive Yuan for circulation to the relevant provinces and regions and the National Government's Water Disaster Committee for adoption and implementation. Resolved to handle it carefully and quickly. 3. The Chief reported that the association handled a small part of the income and expenditure accounts of last year's exhibition. It was proposed to hand them over to the chairman of the exhibition for designation of a special commissioner to review the case. Resolved to hand it over to Cao Yunxiang, acting chairman of the exhibition, for review and transfer to Zheng Xitao, the secretary, for joint audit and publication with the exhibition accounts by the accountant. Approved as is. 4. The Chief reported on the outline of the work plan for next year. The chairman advocated adding three items: (a) Each member must solicit at least ten members next year in order to promote publicity and maintain association affairs; (b) Expedite the completion of the Shanghai-Nanjing Highway and send a letter to the Jiangsu Construction Department to disclose the route plan to the association; (c) Expedite the design of the Wanli Long Dike to make it wider and change it into a Wanli Dike Road in order to benefit farmers and workers and consolidate the dike base. The rest will be carried out actively according to the outline of the plan. The three added items should be given special attention and urged forward at any time. Resolved to comply. Temporary proposals were omitted.

Opening Tomorrow

Public Memorial Service for Xu Fengweng Not to be Held

Xu Jingren Resolutely Declined in Accordance with His Father's Will

Previously, leaders of various charities in the city and celebrities from all walks of life initiated a public memorial service for Xu Yutang Fengweng, scheduled to be held on January 3, 22nd year, at the Buddhist Jingye Society on Hart Road. The call for essays had been published in various newspapers. This time, Chairman Xu Jingren returned to Shanghai from Wuhan and learned of this event. Because he strictly abided by Xu Fengweng's will, which stipulated that during times of national crisis, ceremonies should be simple and frugal, with no mourning and no obituaries, he did not dare to accept the public memorial service initiated by the elders and acquaintances from all walks of life in the city. He has already expressed his most sincere respect and gratitude to the initiators of the public memorial service and resolutely declined. It is planned not to hold the service.

Actress Lin Yongyong Abuses Maid

Charity Society Intervenes to Provide Relief

Lin Yongyong, an actress at the Xinxin Rooftop Garden New Theater, about 30 years old, from Suzhou, lives at 714 and a half, Meifu Lane, Parker Road. During the Shanghai War, she bought a 12-year-old girl named Wang Azhen from the refugees for 120 yuan to be her maid, forcing her to do hard labor and arbitrarily abusing her, even beating her cruelly, which was inhumane. This was heard by the中华慈幼协会 at No. 20 Museum Road. The association immediately sent two staff members, Zhang Yueru and Ding Dongnan, accompanied by a Western detective from the Avenue Road police station, to conduct an on-site investigation. They found that Wang Azhen, the maid, had numerous scars on her face and arms, which they learned were caused by Lin Yongyong hitting her with a ruler. Lin Yongyong was arrested and questioned and the girl was sent to Guangren Hospital for a medical examination. It is reported that she will be handed over to the court for trial at 9 a.m. today.

Da Zhonghua Scientific Research Association Visits Zhanghua Woolen Mill

The Da Zhonghua Scientific Research Association was founded by Wu Zhihui. It has been established for seven years, but has been suspended due to various reasons. It was re-established this summer, focusing on popularizing scientific knowledge and technology, and guiding social production and consumption. Those who join are enthusiastic about science. Yesterday, more than 40 ordinary members of the association in Shanghai, at the invitation of Cheng Nianpeng, the manager of the Zhanghua Woolen Manufacturing Company in Zhoujiadu, crossed the river accompanied by Tong Xinzhi, a senior employee of the company, and Xu Yunzhi, the executive director of the association, to visit the manufacturing process from wool selection to finished products. The engineers of the factory, Xi and Pan, explained the process to them. The members of the association praised the factory's equipment and management. After the visit, they had refreshments in the factory's living room and took a photograph.徐 Yunzhi, the new executive director of the association, told people that Zhanghua was able to spin, weave, and produce finished products without any foreign raw materials, which was truly commendable in the current Chinese wool industry. However, the engine still used steam power, which consumed too much energy, which was a slight drawback. According to the factory, it has decided to switch to electricity next year in order to realize this. They are extremely grateful for Xu's suggestion.

College Student Fang Jiali's Bad Luck Continues

Concubine Sues First, Wife Accuses Later

(Fang's Witty Remarks) Willing to Fill the Yamen with Foreign Money, the Magistrate Only Wants Copper Coins, Plaintiff's Agent Has Already Asked the Court to Record it in the Minutes

(Wife's Request) Wife Requests Divorce, Demands 50,000 Yuan in Alimony, Judge Hopes Both Parties Can Reconcile, Continued Hearing Period Extended

Fang Jiali, a native of this county, is 22 years old, resides at No. 6 Zhengde Lane, South Chengdu Road, and is a graduate of a university in West Shanghai. He possesses a large fortune. In the 19th year of the Republic, he had a relationship with Li Sanyuan (21 years old), a woman from Jiaozhi, Suzhou, at No. 27 Xicheng Lane, Ximen Road. He then rented a house in the French Concession at No. 12 Guifu Lane, Taiping Bridge, and No. 38 Juxing Lane, Beidi Road, and lived together. In September of this year, their relationship suddenly broke down, causing Li's mother to sue Fang for seduction and abandonment in the Criminal Court of the First Special Court, demanding payment of 30,000 yuan for living expenses. However, one wave subsided, and another rose. Recently, Fang's

Legal Wife Cai Huiying

Also because Fang smoked opium, contracted a venereal disease, and was unbearable to abuse, hired lawyers Gu Xianzhang and others to file a complaint in the Civil Court of the First Special Court, requesting a divorce and demanding 50,000 yuan in alimony. The complaint stated that the plaintiff, on the eighth day of the first month of the 20th year of the Republic, married Fang Jiali, a wealthy man, at the behest of her parents and through the mediation of Shen Chenghua and Yang Ruheng. He Would Take Away the Plaintiff's Jewelry

He did not care about the plaintiff's food, clothing, housing, and other expenses. People were full of rumors, saying that the defendant had a lover before marrying the plaintiff. Because it was during the honeymoon period, she did not want to accuse him of this kind of baseless talk, which would lead to an irreparable rift in their relationship. Knowing that the wind comes from an empty cave, it is definitely not without reason, but she still hoped that he would stray from the right path and eventually change his ways, so that they could grow old together. However, she did not expect the defendant to have made it a habit. He already

Was Indulging in Opium

When she tried to dissuade him, he dared to threaten her with a pistol. In this dangerous situation, if the plaintiff continued to compromise, her health would be a concern. Problem of Restoring Electricity

Questioning How the Power Company Can Determine and Execute Penalties on its Own

Looking Back, the Municipal Council Still Sought Punishment from the Court, Emphasizing the Rule of Law

The Taxpayers' Association sent another letter to the Municipal Council urging the restoration of electricity to Laoyan Maoyuan, stating: We are writing to you on behalf of the Shanghai Citizens' Federation, regarding a letter from member Laoyan Maoyuan Liquor Store, claiming that our store was falsely accused by the Shanghai Power Company of tampering with the electricity meter and was ordered to pay an additional electricity fee of over two thousand taels. Because we believed this was unreasonable harassment, they cut off our electricity on November 11, causing significant business losses. We have previously requested the Shanghai Ratepayers' Association to uphold fairness and justice, and the association has forwarded a letter to the Municipal Council requesting a stop to this action, and the Municipal Council has also sent a letter to the power company requesting correction. However, many days have passed, and the power company has not complied, nor has the Municipal Council taken any action. This delay is causing even greater losses. Therefore, we are requesting your association to forward another letter to the Shanghai Ratepayers' Association, urging the Municipal Council to expedite the negotiation to maintain business interests, and so on. According to our investigation, since Laoyan Maoyuan installed the electricity meter, the company has sent a specialist to read the meter every month, and until the final removal, there were no claims of tampering with the meter's lead seals. The meter was taken to the company, and only after several days did this accusation arise. Even if there were traces of tampering, it is impossible to prove whether they were interchanged with other meters or fabricated, and Laoyan Maoyuan cannot be held responsible. If it is claimed that the difference in electricity usage, past and present, raises suspicion of fraud, the business of a store fluctuates, and the amount of electricity used naturally varies. The current meter reading cannot be used as a standard for past electricity usage. Moreover, electricity is a public utility, and the public interest should be the priority. If the company can do whatever it wants, demand whatever it wants, and disregard the public interest simply because it is a monopoly, that is unreasonable. The company's forceful cutoff of electricity is not in line with proper practices. Based on the aforementioned situation, we are forwarding this letter to your association, requesting you to immediately urge the Municipal Council to order the Shanghai Power Company to restore the electricity supply to Laoyan Maoyuan to maintain business interests. We have previously sent a letter to your bureau requesting an investigation, but no results have been received to date, resulting in significant business losses for the store. The Shanghai Power Company determines and executes penalties on its own, leaving no room for taxpayers to voice their grievances or seek redress. We wonder what effective measures your bureau, which is responsible for safeguarding the legal rights of taxpayers, has to correct this barbaric and oppressive behavior. We recall that during the time when the power company was managed by the Electricity Department of your bureau, a certain Lin used illegal procedures, and the case was brought to the Mixed Court for punishment. Your bureau, as the local administrative authority, still emphasized the rule of law and did not determine and execute penalties on its own. If this situation is not promptly corrected administratively (since the company's actions constitute direct action, the administration should be responsible for correction), all the characteristics of the rule of law within the concession will be completely destroyed by the company. This is a serious matter. Based on the aforementioned reasons, we are writing to your bureau, requesting you to promptly order the Shanghai Power Company to restore the electricity supply to the store. Addressed to the Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement.

The Shanghai Race Club and other organizations formed a disaster relief racing affairs department, issuing 100,000 special prize tickets for the International Charity Horse Race, priced at ten silver dollars each, to aid the disaster victims in northern Shanghai. Miserable Death of a Tent Keeper on a Road Under Repair

Three Men in Short Clothes Wielding Sharp Axes

Four Axe Blows Cost a Life

Yesterday morning at 3:30 AM, an assassination occurred at the intersection of Beijing Road and Fujian Road. Recently, the Municipal Council dispatched road workers to repair the road at that location. After the workers finished for the night, an individual, Mr. Jia, around fifty years old, was assigned to guard all the road construction equipment inside a tent beside the road. At approximately 3:30 AM yesterday morning, three men wearing short clothes suddenly appeared, wielding sharp axes. Catching Mr. Jia off guard, they attacked him with the axes. Mr. Jia fell to the ground in extreme pain. Seeing that their objective had been achieved, the assailants fled. Later, a Chinese constable, number 3057, patrolled by the area and discovered the incident. Seeing that Mr. Jia was unconscious, he urgently transported him to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, due to the severity of his injuries, he soon died. The hospital reported the incident to the police, who transported the body to the coroner's office for examination and to investigate the deceased's name and family and to pursue the murderers. Later, it was learned that the deceased was Tian Dexin from Tianjin, 56 years old, wearing a black cotton-padded coat and trousers, with an old Western-style coat over it, and a velvet hat. He was struck by four axe blows, on the top of the head, left cheek, left back of the head, and nose, with the blow to the top of the head being the most severe, causing his death.

Walking in a Desolate Grave in the Middle of the Night

Begging Repeatedly to Avoid Death

Zhu Yan, a Woman from Jiaxing, Has a Fateful Destiny

Liu Hongkui Commits All Kinds of Evil and Should Be Severely Punished

Zhu Yan, a 37-year-old woman from Jiaxing, currently residing at No. 10 Huiyuan Lane, Kunshan Road, was escorted by a fellow townsman to the 3rd precinct of the 5th district to file a complaint. She stated that in June of this year, the defendant lured her to Shanghai from Jiaxing under the pretense of taking her to a used goods store, and brought her nine-year-old daughter with her. However, the defendant pawned all of Ms. Zhu's capital and clothing. In August, due to financial constraints, Ms. Zhu was sold to Luzhou, Anhui. Her nine-year-old daughter was taken by the defendant's wife. At that time, the defendant lived on Huade Road. Because Ms. Zhu could not bear the hardship, she escaped to Shanghai in August. When she went to the defendant's residence to look for her daughter, she was nowhere to be found. When she questioned him, the defendant lied to her that the daughter was in Pudong and led Ms. Zhu to Gaolang Bridge, specifically walking through graveyards and deserted areas, claiming it was a shortcut. It was already 11 PM. The defendant took out a long rope and tied up Ms. Zhu, intending to harm her. Ms. Zhu begged repeatedly, appealing to their previous relationship and promising not to seek her daughter again. The defendant then released Ms. Zhu. Unexpectedly, the next day, he lured her again, saying that her daughter was now in Bengbu, just to scare her, and they could go together to pick her up. So they took the Datong steamer to Bengbu, and then he took her to Liu Township, more than a hundred li away, and sold her to an old man named Liu Changshun to be his wife. Because Ms. Zhu cried incessantly, Liu felt sympathetic and sent her to Nanjing to find relatives before returning to Shanghai. Therefore, she arrested the defendant and requested a severe punishment. When questioned, the defendant was evasive. Because the case was extremely complex, it was transferred to the local court for investigation.

Photographer Li Hanzhong Dies on the Battlefield

In Order to Capture the History of the Northeastern Volunteer Army's Resistance Against Japan, Jinan Film Company Specially Sent Huang Huaisheng's Younger Brother Jianping and Photographers Ding Wenzhi and Li Hanzhong, Three People, to the Front Line in Mid-August. Reader's Advisor

Ms. Wu Asks: Mr. So-and-so and I developed from friendship to love, and it has been more than three years. Last year, we asked two teachers, the director of academic affairs and the Chinese teacher of a certain middle school, to introduce us and establish a marriage contract (we are both already eighteen years old, and according to the newly announced law, we have the right to freely choose a spouse). Each of us holds one copy, and in the future, neither party can change it. This year, we asked someone to discuss it with my father, but he refused to agree. Alas! I am really in a dilemma. If I carry out our marriage contract, I will be disobeying my parents' orders. If I obey my parents' orders, Mr. So-and-so has put in a lot of effort for me, and if I change my mind halfway, wouldn't I be doing him wrong in my conscience? Gentlemen! I have discussed it with my father, but it didn't work. Now I want the marriage contract to be carried out, as long as my father and I don't have any disagreements, and we can still be happy. Father and daughter are father and daughter, husband and wife are husband and wife. What method can be used to start?

Answer: The question in the letter can be answered in two points:

(1) Legal Aspects: According to the current Civil Code, "A minor entering into a marriage contract shall obtain the consent of his or her legal representative." Although the woman was already eighteen years old when she entered into the marriage contract, according to Article 12 of the Civil Code: "Full twenty years of age is adulthood," the woman is still a "minor." A minor is a "person with limited capacity for conduct," and "a unilateral act performed by a person with limited capacity for conduct without the permission of his or her legal representative is invalid" (Article 78 of the same law). Therefore, the woman's marriage contract with the other party is invalid because it has not been consented to by her parents (legal representatives). Legally speaking, this marriage contract is really not firm. However, there is also considerable relief. No. 598,

"After a divorce by mutual consent, the father shall be responsible for the custody of the children, but if there is a separate agreement, that agreement shall be followed." Now that A and B have divorced by mutual consent, regarding the custody of the children, since there is an agreement, the agreement should be followed according to the law. However, since B is in financial difficulty and unable to support the child, who has been sent to an orphanage, A can certainly demand that B fulfill the obligation to provide support based on Article 1114 of the Civil Code (stating that direct blood relatives have a mutual obligation to provide support) and Article 1117 (stating that those eligible for support are limited to those who cannot maintain their livelihoods and lack the ability to earn a living). Otherwise, A can file a lawsuit in court, because a mother who has been married still cannot have her obligation to support her child extinguished simply because there is a separate agreement regarding custody.

Mr. Hu Dingsheng inquires: Our clan has a sacrificial property that has been passed down for over two hundred years, consisting of only three mu of land, managed by A and B in alternating years. Now, B only has one member, who is only engaged in wandering and does not engage in any proper work. Recently, B wants to sell half of the land to someone. (1) This land forms a single plot and has not been divided. Which side belongs to B? (2) If A does not sign, can B sell it alone?

Reply: As described in your letter, the sacrificial property managed by A and B in alternating years is legally called "jointly owned property." According to Article 823 of the Civil Code, each co-owner may request division at any time. The method of division can be determined by agreement. If the land can be divided, it should be equally divided by agreement. If it cannot be divided, then it can only be sold, and the proceeds divided equally. However, if A does not sign, B cannot sell it alone, because according to Article 819 of the Civil Code, the disposal, alteration, and imposition of burdens on jointly owned property must have the consent of all co-owners.

Special Article

A Plea for National Middle Schools (1)

— Liao Maoru

Since the establishment of the National Government, the middle school curriculum has been revised three times. The first time was in 1929, when the Ministry of Education convened a meeting to formulate provisional curriculum standards, which were promulgated and implemented in August of that year. In 1930, the provisional standards were revised again after deliberation by the Ministry of Education. In August of this year, the Ministry of Education convened another meeting to revise the curriculum standards for senior and junior high schools, setting the number of teaching and self-study hours per week for each subject in each semester for senior and junior high schools, which was approved through deliberation and announced in various newspapers. An official order was issued to the education departments of various provinces and cities to instruct all senior and junior high schools under their jurisdiction to implement the timetable promulgated this time in the next semester. Compared with the subject table and credit table of the provisional standards, there are several major differences: (1) Increased weekly teaching time; (2) Eliminated the separation of arts and sciences; (3) Eliminated elective subjects; (4) Eliminated the credit system. This issue is too important to middle schools, and we must raise several points of practical difficulty and request the Ministry of Education to consider them.

1. Too Much Weekly Teaching Time

The school system promulgated in the early Qing Dynasty stipulated 36 hours of teaching per week. In the early years of the Republic of China, not only was the duration of middle school graduation reduced by one year, but the weekly teaching time was also reduced by two or three hours, giving students more opportunities for self-study. This cannot but be said to be a sign of progress. In April of the eighth year of the Republic, the Ministry of Education approved the "adjustment of subjects and time at the discretion of local circumstances" for middle schools. As a result, schools adopted the elective system, stipulating that senior high schools should take 25 credits per semester, which has not changed much until now. The provisional curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry of Education last time also used 26 credits per semester as the standard for senior high schools. The Ministry of Education's advisory document in the eighth year of the Republic truly opened a new era for middle school education in our country. The author has never left middle school administrative life for a single day since the eighth year of the Republic, and has considerable experience to contribute regarding the disputes over the elective system, the advantages and disadvantages of the departmental system, the addition and subtraction of subjects, and the allocation of teaching time. I remember when I was at the East China Normal University High School, we often felt that the students were too busy and said, "You can't have your cake and eat it too. There's no such thing as having both, but school administrators often have such extravagant hopes for students." On the one hand, we want students to read more reference books, do more homework, and visit more places in person. On the other hand, we also want them to exercise more, train their bodies, participate in more extracurricular activities, improve their ability to handle affairs, and develop sound personalities. When I arrived at Guanghua High School, I still had the same feeling, especially for the students in the second and third years of senior high school, none of them didn't say they were busy. But we still forced them to participate in various activities, such as cleaning competitions, current affairs tests, subject tests, group activities, editing special issues, speech contests, ball games, excursions, field trips, research conferences, concerts, sports meets, and teacher-student social gatherings. Because we don't want a young person to come to middle school to become a bookworm and turn into a pretentious, knowledge-stuffed Confucian scholar. However, although students are busy, their interest in their studies is still not weak. If we remove all extracurricular activities and force them to become bookworms, not only will they not study well, but they will also feel that life is dry and monotonous, which will cause inexplicable boredom and unrest. I often think about how we can extract the essentials of middle school teaching materials, concentrate training, reduce students' class time, and increase their practical work, so as to cultivate a large number of young people who are "capable and principled." I have cherished this ideal for many years, but I never thought that the Ministry of Education would go against it and greatly increase the teaching time in middle schools. Putting aside experience, and speaking from the perspective of modern trends, middle schools in the United States are now reducing teaching time, with junior high schools reducing to about 23 hours a week and senior high schools reducing to about 21 hours a week. The current timetable in our country requires junior high schools to have 35-36 hours of classes per week, and senior high schools to have 33-34 hours of classes per week. The gentlemen at the meeting seemed to only care about increasing the time for each subject, without considering the requirements of the times and the abilities of the students. What are the requirements of the times? That is, schools should promote labor, promote extracurricular activities, and promote automatic learning. However, all of these require time. According to that timetable, students can only be busy listening to lectures all day long. Where can they have enough time to study on their own, research, work, or participate in extracurricular activities? Putting aside the facts, and speaking from the discussions of Chinese and foreign educators on education in our country, Mr. Zhuang Zeyan criticized many aspects of modern middle schools in his book "How to Sinicize New Education." He said, "The number of subjects in general middle schools is so large that it makes people who don't know education or are new to school dizzy. Middle school students are truly the darlings of heaven. One moment there is a teacher to talk about geography, the next moment there is a teacher to talk about history, the next moment there is a teacher to talk about physics, the next moment there is a teacher to talk about chemistry... Those who like to listen can listen, and it doesn't matter if they don't listen. After one class, there is a ten-minute break to chat, smoke cigarettes, eat Western pastries..." He advocates that only the essential points of the current curriculum should be retained for teachers to teach, and students should focus on work or investigation. In addition, time should be spent on self-study under the guidance of teachers. This point is quite in line with the author's feelings. Mr. Liang Shuming said in his speech "The Direction of Middle School Transformation in the Future," "Today's students only stand in a passive and receptive position, as if they regard the student era as a short-term preparatory era for life, an era dedicated to reading, thinking that if others prepare everything for them properly, they can concentrate on reading, but the result is completely different. Not only can they not study well and cannot seek knowledge, but they also turn themselves into useless people who cannot do anything. The original intention of education is to cultivate people with skills and abilities. If you want to make a person skilled and capable, you must develop their senses, thoughts, hands, and feet." Therefore, Mr. Liang implemented a method of life education and automatic education in the school. We are very sympathetic to Mr. Liang's words. Recently, the conclusion of the League of Nations special education investigation team's visit to China also said that middle schools have too much teaching time, and many middle schools have too much mental work, which leads to students being irritable and uneasy. There is too little entertainment and outdoor activities, too little close contact between teachers and students, and too little training in group life to bear social responsibility. The method to eliminate this drawback is very simple in foreign countries. We must remember that children should first be treated as children and then as students. Therefore, school life must not only meet the needs of children's minds but also adapt to their multifaceted nature. In terms of implementation, the relationship between teachers and students should not be too serious and too distant. Students should be encouraged to organize various gatherings and manage themselves. Older and capable students should be given appropriate powers so that they have the opportunity to practice maintaining order and handling school affairs. Extracurricular activities occupy an important, sometimes very important, position in school life. Although the methods used in other countries do not necessarily have to be transplanted to China in their entirety, we believe that China will always be able to find a method suitable for China's situation." This passage is very thorough.

Junior High School Curriculum Standards (7)

Botany

I. Objectives

(1) To understand the relationship between plants and human life;

(2) To understand the fundamental principles and facts of botany;

(3) To recognize local and common applied plants;

(4) To arouse interest in cultivating, collecting, and studying plants;

(5) To obtain preliminary training in collecting and cultivating plants;

(6) To cultivate a love of appreciating plants;

(7) To cultivate the ability to observe automatically.

II. Time Allocation

To be taught in the first year of junior high school, with two hours of lectures per week. Practical exercises should be held for two hours each time outside of class, under the guidance of the responsible teacher.

III. Teaching Material Outline

(1) The fundamental organization and function of plants, such as cells and tissues;

(2) A discussion of the morphology, structure, and living methods of roots, stems, flowers, fruits, and seeds;

(3) When discussing each part, attention should be paid to anything related to human life. For example, when discussing roots and soil, the meaning of farmland cultivation and fertilization should be shown, as well as the uses of roots, etc. When discussing stems, the importance of forests and the uses of fibers, etc., should be included. When discussing leaves, the source of starch and sugars produced by grains, etc., should be included. When discussing flowers and seeds, the methods and significance of plant breeding, etc., should be included.

(4) Outline of plant classification. This section accounts for about one-quarter of the teaching material and only provides a brief description of the major categories of plants in the order of natural evolution to show the order of development. The plants used as examples for each category should be useful, harmful, and commonly seen plants. Examples are as follows:

(1) Lower plants... Spirogyra, Volvox, bacteria, Aspergillus, Rhizopus, brewer's yeast, mushrooms, liverwort, moss, ferns, water clover, etc. (2) Higher plants. (A) Agricultural plants... Rice, wheat, millet, sorghum, corn, peach, pear, persimmon, orange, grape, cabbage, mustard greens, water chestnut, spinach, potato, taro, lotus root, arrowhead, sweet potato, radish, eggplant, cucurbits, soybeans, broad beans, or peas, etc. (B) Daily use plants, fibrous raw materials... Cotton, ramie, mulberry, etc. Oil paint raw materials... tung oil, soybean, peanut, hemp, lacquer tree, tung tree, etc. Dyes... safflower, etc. Craft materials... bamboo, rattan, camphor, rush, etc. (C) Medicinal plants and stimulants. Medicinal materials... mint, pinellia, fennel, rhubarb, ginseng, plantain, almond, licorice, pyrethrum, etc. Spices... pepper, ginger, mustard, etc. Drinks... tea. Smoking materials... tobacco. (D) Forests... poplar, willow, pine, cypress, oak, chestnut, etc. (E) Ornamental plants... peony, chrysanthemum, hollyhock, dianthus, iris, narcissus, magnolia, Cymbidium, etc. (F) Harmful plants, poisonous plants... Euphorbia, buttercup, etc. Parasitic plants... dodder, mistletoe, etc. Field weeds... beggar ticks, crabgrass, etc. All of the above plants should be arranged in the order of classification, but teachers can make appropriate additions and subtractions based on local products. (Note) The following points should be noted when compiling teaching materials:

(1) The compilation of teaching materials must be connected and orderly;

(2) Botany in junior high school should pay attention to the fundamental principles of plant life and its relationship with human life everywhere. The selection of materials should not be limited by pure botany;

(3) Plants are whole, and their blessing is also whole. The compilation should be listed separately, but at all times there should be an impression of cooperation between the various parts;

(4) Morphology, structure, and life have a close relationship. When compiling, morphology and living methods should be combined into one, and should not be discussed separately. This method can not only clarify the meaning of morphology, but also increase students' interest.

IV. Summary of Implementation Methods

(1) Homework Requirements

(1) Observation; (2) Experiment; (3) Collection and preparation of specimens; (4) Recording and drawing.

(2) Teaching Method Key Points

Take nature as the teaching text, and the teacher should enlighten from the side. Books are only used to supplement the lack of observation and experimentation, and should not occupy the primary position.

Dr. Chen Yaodong Returns Home After Completing His Studies

Mr. Chen Yaodong, having studied in Europe for nearly six years, returned to China on the 10th of this month aboard a French postal ship. After graduating from the Department of Political Science and Economics at Southeast University, Mr. Chen went to the Faculty of Law at the University of Paris in France. In 1929, he obtained a Master of Laws degree. In the same year, he entered the graduate school of the same university and subsequently obtained higher diplomas in public law and private law. Last winter, Mr. Chen submitted a dissertation and passed with honors, whereupon the French Ministry of Education awarded him a national Doctor of Laws degree. He then went to England to study international law at the University of London. His book, "A Comparative Study of the Abolition of Consular Jurisdiction of Eastern Countries," published by the Parisian Sirey Bookstore (Receuil Sirey), has been very well received. The International Law Association, finding many original insights in the book, elected Mr. Chen as a formal member at its annual meeting in Oxford, England, this August, a truly commendable achievement. During his time in Europe, Mr. Chen also devoted considerable effort to anti-Japanese propaganda, giving speeches or debates in England and France more than twenty times. In Paris, he received several warnings from the police to leave the country, indicating the intensity of his rhetoric. During his time in France, he interned at the Paris Court for one year. Last spring, Ms. Luo Heng from Yunnan accidentally injured a French woman while driving in Paris, and Mr. Chen successfully defended her in court. Mr. Chen plans to use his experience in dealing with foreigners during his time in Europe to practice law in Shanghai, specializing in Chinese-foreign lawsuits to protect the interests of the people and safeguard national rights. Mr. Chen has traveled to more than ten countries, including Germany, Russia, Switzerland, the Netherlands, and Italy, and is fluent in the languages of various countries. He is expected to be competent and successful in handling Chinese-foreign lawsuits and safeguarding civil rights in the future.
